### [101+ Famous Thinkers on Owning Earth](https://www.progress.org/articles/101-famous-thinkers-on-owning-earth/)
- **supports** [`narratives/the-great-land-robbery`](https://progress.org/wiki/the-great-land-robbery/) — anchor: **“Owning Earth differs from owning wealth”**
  - sentence: …Owning Earth differs from owning wealth in four fundamental ways: Making something (investing our labor) lets us own the thing.…
  - why: The essay's opening argument that land is distinct from man-made wealth because it is not produced by labor directly supports the narrative that land titles are based on enclosure rather than producti
- **supports** [`narratives/community-creates-land-value`](https://progress.org/wiki/community-creates-land-value/) — anchor: **“users pay compensation to those they exclude”**
  - sentence: …They reached this conclusion by reasoning from the uniqueness of land: users pay compensation to those they exclude.…
  - why: This phrase encapsulates the essay's reasoning that land value arises from the community's need for access (which owners exclude), grounding the ethical claim that value is socially created.
- **supports** [`narratives/unearned-increment-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/unearned-increment-narrative/) — anchor: **“The most comfortable, but also the most unproductive way”**
  - sentence: …The most comfortable, but also the most unproductive way for a capitalist to increase his fortune, is to put all monies in sites and await that point in time when a society, hungering for land, has to pay his price.…
  - why: Carnegie's quote illustrates the moral argument that landowners gain wealth passively through the 'unearned increment' generated by society's growth rather than their own effort.
- **supports** [`narratives/land-speculation-causes-cycles`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-speculation-causes-cycles/) — anchor: **“Waiting for higher future prices”**
  - sentence: …Waiting for higher future prices, some owners withhold sites, worsening the land price spiral.…
  - why: The essay explicitly identifies the mechanism of withholding land for speculative gain as a driver of price spirals, supporting the narrative that land speculation causes economic instability.

### [A Georgist Approach to Emissions Rights](https://www.progress.org/articles/a-georgist-approach-to-emissions-rights/)
- **supports** [`narratives/ecological-rent`](https://progress.org/wiki/ecological-rent/) — anchor: **“scarce natural resource”**
  - sentence: …The analytical claim is that we should think about the atmosphere—specifically, its ability to absorb greenhouse gasses—as a scarce natural resource that commands an economic rent.…
  - why: The essay explicitly frames the atmosphere's absorption capacity as a scarce natural resource commanding economic rent, which is the core definition of ecological rent.
- **supports** [`benefits/carbon-pricing-cuts-emissions`](https://progress.org/wiki/carbon-pricing-cuts-emissions/) — anchor: **“shift the economic burden”**
  - sentence: …International climate negotiations aim to gradually shift the economic burden from future generations to the present generation, by raising the cost of emitting.…
  - why: The essay argues for pricing emissions to internalize the externality, supporting the claim that carbon pricing mechanisms effectively shift the burden of climate costs.
- **supports** [`narratives/unearned-increment-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/unearned-increment-narrative/) — anchor: **“collect this economic rent”**
  - sentence: …Currently, people who emit greenhouse gasses by burning fossil fuels collect this economic rent because most countries do not impose carbon taxes, and the countries that do set them too low.…
  - why: The essay describes the collection of economic rent from a common resource (the atmosphere) by private actors without payment, illustrating the concept of the unearned increment.
- **supports** [`narratives/citizens-dividend-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/citizens-dividend-narrative/) — anchor: **“socialize the natural resource rents”**
  - sentence: …George’s approach is to socialize the natural resource rents and let everyone in the community have an equal share of them.…
  - why: The essay contrasts Lockean appropriation with George's approach to socialize rents and share them equally, which is the foundational argument for the citizens' dividend narrative.

### [A German State Quietly Implemented a Land Value Tax](https://www.progress.org/articles/a-german-state-quietly-implemented-a-land-value-tax/)

  - sentence: …The experience is still young and the tax rate still small, but it sets a precedent: land value taxes are not politically impossible.…
  - why: The essay presents a major contemporary implementation in a German state as a direct counterexample to the objection that LVT is never adopted.
- **supports** [`benefits/lvt-reduces-sprawl`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-reduces-sprawl/) — anchor: **“incentive to be careful”**
  - sentence: …“The Green Party found it very appealing because the land value tax is a tax which gives an incentive to be careful with the scarce resource of land.”…
  - why: The essay cites the Green Party's support for LVT specifically because it encourages efficient land use and compact development, which counters sprawl.
- **counters** [`objections/lvt-is-just-a-property-tax`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-is-just-a-property-tax/) — anchor: **“taxing land value alone”**
  - sentence: …In 2025, Baden-Württemberg – a German state of 11 million residents – implemented a land value tax . Instead of taxing both land and buildings, it taxes land value alone.…
  - why: The essay explicitly contrasts the new German system with standard property taxes, highlighting the shift to taxing land alone to refute the claim that they are identical.
- **counters** [`objections/lvt-needs-zoning-reform-first`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-needs-zoning-reform-first/) — anchor: **“opted out of the federal framework”**
  - sentence: …Baden-Württemberg opted out of the federal framework entirely. On January 1, 2025, the Grundsteuer there began taxing land value alone.…
  - why: The essay describes a successful implementation of LVT without first establishing that zoning reform was a prerequisite, countering the objection that LVT is useless without it.

  - sentence: …Much of that rent should be distributed in equal shares of money.…
  - why: The essay argues that distributing land rent equally abolishes poverty and inequality, directly supporting the claim that rent dividends reduce poverty.
- **supports** [`benefits/congestion-pricing-reduces-traffic`](https://progress.org/wiki/congestion-pricing-reduces-traffic/) — anchor: **“tolls just high enough”**
  - sentence: …The pollution of traffic from congestion is similarly handled with tolls just high enough to prevent crowding.…
  - why: The essay proposes using tolls to prevent traffic crowding, which substantively supports the claim that congestion pricing reduces traffic.

  - why: Shearman argues that taxing unearned income is a necessary and immediate fiscal reform, independent of other structural changes like zoning.

### [About Interest](https://www.progress.org/articles/about-interest/)
- **supports** [`narratives/land-speculation-causes-cycles`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-speculation-causes-cycles/) — anchor: **“cheap credit generates real estate booms”**
  - sentence: …The cheap credit generates real estate booms that end in a financial crisis and depression when land values become unaffordable, and, as the money stops expanding, when interest rates go back up.…
  - why: The essay argues that central bank money expansion pushes interest rates below the natural rate, inducing borrowing for real estate and causing boom-bust cycles.
- **supports** [`problems/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land`](https://progress.org/wiki/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land/) — anchor: **“Public goods make locations more attractive”**
  - sentence: …Another distortion in interest rates is government subsidies to land values: Public goods make locations more attractive and productive, increasing land rent and land values because the goods are paid mostly from taxes on wages and goods.…
  - why: The essay explains that public investment increases land values, which then fuels speculative borrowing.
- **counters** [`objections/cycles-are-credit-not-land`](https://progress.org/wiki/cycles-are-credit-not-land/) — anchor: **“This artificially cheap credit induces more borrowing”**
  - sentence: …The money expansion pushes the transaction rate of interest, the rate paid by borrowers, below the natural rate: This artificially cheap credit induces more borrowing for goods of long duration, especially real estate.…
  - why: While acknowledging credit drives the cycle, the essay argues the mechanism is specifically credit flowing into land speculation due to subsidies, countering the view that land is irrelevant.
- **counters** [`objections/land-is-just-capital`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-is-just-capital/) — anchor: **“just as rent is the yield of land”**
  - sentence: …But just as rent is the yield of land aside from any interest for borrowing, the capital yield from buildings, tools, and inventory is aside from any interest.…
  - why: The essay explicitly distinguishes the yield of land (rent) from the yield of capital goods and loaned funds (interest), refuting the conflation of land with capital.

### [Abundance and Anti-Monopoly: The Legacy of Tom Johnson](https://www.progress.org/articles/abundance-and-anti-monopoly-the-legacy-of-tom-johnson/)
- **illustrates** [`narratives/progressive-era-georgism`](https://progress.org/wiki/progressive-era-georgism/) — anchor: **“Tom Johnson united anti-monopoly”**
  - sentence: …Tom Johnson united anti-monopoly and abundance and serves as a model for what an authentically anti-monopolist abundance movement might look like.…
  - why: The essay uses Tom Johnson's career as a case study of Georgist influence during the Progressive Era.
- **illustrates** [`narratives/single-tax-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/single-tax-narrative/) — anchor: **“devoted his life to the single-tax”**
  - sentence: …After reading Henry George ’s Progress and Poverty , he devoted his life to the single-tax—a confiscatory tax on land values that would redistribute rent to ensure that everyone had access to a high standard of living.…
  - why: It details Johnson's adoption of the Single Tax as a core political philosophy.
- **illustrates** [`problems/rent-seeking-drags-growth`](https://progress.org/wiki/rent-seeking-drags-growth/) — anchor: **“courts and cumbersome process impeded democracy”**
  - sentence: …But if there was one stand that ran throughout, it was that courts and cumbersome process impeded democracy and empowered special interests.…
  - why: It illustrates how legal obstructionism and monopoly privileges hinder democratic progress and economic abundance.
- **supports** [`narratives/community-creates-land-value`](https://progress.org/wiki/community-creates-land-value/) — anchor: **“fruits of progress accrued only to those”**
  - sentence: …Without redistribution, rent would ensure that the fruits of progress accrued only to those who already owned land, natural resources, or monopolistic businesses like railroads.…
  - why: It supports the Georgist argument that community-driven progress creates land value that is captured by rentiers.

### [Accounting (unearned) Profit vs. Economic (earned) Profit](https://www.progress.org/articles/accounting-unearned-profit-vs-economic-earned-profit/)
- **supports** [`problems/corporate-profits-increasingly-rents`](https://progress.org/wiki/corporate-profits-increasingly-rents/) — anchor: **“ACCOUNTING PROFIT of business”**
  - sentence: …The ACCOUNTING PROFIT of business, representing the excess of income over cost . . . has nothing to do with economics.…
  - why: Foulke argues that corporate accounting profits conflate true returns to capital with economic rent from land, supporting the claim that modern profits are largely rents.
- **counters** [`objections/land-is-just-capital`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-is-just-capital/) — anchor: **“ACCOUNTING PROFITS of corporations”**
  - sentence: …The reason is that the ACCOUNTING PROFITS of corporations, which own land where some of their plants, warehouses or other installations are located, actually encompass ECONOMIC RENT.…
  - why: The essay disputes the conflation of land and capital by demonstrating that accounting profits artificially merge land rent with capital returns.
- **supports** [`objections/land-cannot-be-assessed`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-cannot-be-assessed/) — anchor: **“separate the naked value of land”** ⚠️ *ungrounded anchor*
  - sentence: …Moreover we lack even a faint idea to what represents value on the value of land in its natural state and what part represents the return on capital invested in a business which includes improvements on the land.…
  - why: The text explicitly identifies the practical difficulty of separating land value from capital improvements in corporate accounting.
- **supports** [`objections/taxing-quasi-rents-kills-innovation`](https://progress.org/wiki/taxing-quasi-rents-kills-innovation/) — anchor: **“highly efficient capital items”**
  - sentence: …An interesting problem arises in our technological era where capital goods (computers, robots, electronics, etc.) are becoming so efficient.…
  - why: The essay grapples with whether returns from advanced technology constitute earned interest or unearned gains, addressing the innovation objection.

### [AFFEERCE Georgism (part 1)](https://www.progress.org/articles/affeerce-georgism-part-1/)
- **supports** [`problems/land-rent-could-fund-government`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-rent-could-fund-government/) — anchor: **“supply each of us with”**
  - sentence: …Because it can supply each of us with nutritious meals, warm and safe shelter, quality medical care, unlimited free education, police and fire protection, a government to protect our rights, streets and sanitation, and so forth, it must!…
  - why: The essay argues that the land's capacity to provide for all human needs implies that land rent is sufficient to fund essential government services and public goods.
- **supports** [`narratives/community-creates-land-value`](https://progress.org/wiki/community-creates-land-value/) — anchor: **“value is created not through”**
  - sentence: …Land, a gift of God or Nature, and whose value is created not through the effort of any one individual, but rather by the very presence of a community, cannot be owned.…
  - why: The essay explicitly states that land value is generated by the community rather than individual effort, which is the core definition of this narrative.
- **supports** [`narratives/single-tax-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/single-tax-narrative/) — anchor: **“Businesses are freed from the tyranny”**
  - sentence: …Businesses are freed from the tyranny of taxation and voluntarily bid on the best land to rent, as today they would bid on the best land to either rent or purchase.…
  - why: The essay describes a system where businesses pay rent to the community instead of taxes, illustrating the Single Tax mechanism of shifting the tax burden onto land.
- **counters** [`objections/overpopulation-causes-poverty`](https://progress.org/wiki/overpopulation-causes-poverty/) — anchor: **“An excess population can further”**
  - sentence: …An excess population can further the destruction of the planet, further dehumanization, increase poverty and decrease freedom.…
  - why: The essay acknowledges the Malthusian objection that overpopulation causes poverty but frames it as a specific internal flaw to be solved within the AFFEERCE system rather than a fundamental refutatio

### [AFFEERCE Georgism (part 2)](https://www.progress.org/articles/affeerce-georgism-part-2/)
- **supports** [`problems/land-rent-could-fund-government`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-rent-could-fund-government/) — anchor: **“increased ground rents”**
  - sentence: …To the victor goes the land. To the vanquished goes 150% of the ODV on improvements. To the people go increased ground rents: the spoils of trebler war.…
  - why: The essay proposes a mechanism where captured ground rents are distributed to the people, illustrating how land rent can fund public entitlements.
- **supports** [`benefits/lvt-dampens-land-speculation`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-dampens-land-speculation/) — anchor: **“Without intervention by the land owner”**
  - sentence: …Without intervention by the land owner, ground rents are designed to fall by 10%/year.…
  - why: The essay describes a system where land rents automatically decline if not actively bid up, discouraging passive holding and speculation.
- **supports** [`benefits/land-value-tax-can-be-progressive`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-value-tax-can-be-progressive/) — anchor: **“every person receives a $370 housing distribution”**
  - sentence: …Because every person receives a $370 housing distribution, which can be used for ground rent, apartment rent, mortgages, utilities and renovations, I estimate that 95% of the population will pay nothing of their own money for rent.…
  - why: The essay argues that capturing land value allows for a universal dividend that disproportionately benefits the poor, making the system progressive.

### [AFFEERCE Georgism (part 3)](https://www.progress.org/articles/affeerce-georgism-part-3/)
- **counters** [`objections/lvt-destroys-its-own-tax-base`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-destroys-its-own-tax-base/) — anchor: **“LVT collected will tend toward zero”**
  - sentence: …LVT collected will tend toward zero over time.…
  - why: The essay explicitly argues that LVT revenue collapses over time, directly supporting the objection that the tax destroys its own base.

- **supports** [`objections/land-cannot-be-assessed`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-cannot-be-assessed/) — anchor: **“no objective measure to determine land value”**
  - sentence: …When the price of the land is less than the variance on its improvements, there is no objective measure to determine land value.…
  - why: The essay provides a specific technical argument regarding the difficulty of separating land value from improvement value when improvements are volatile.
- **supports** [`objections/lvt-needs-zoning-reform-first`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-needs-zoning-reform-first/) — anchor: **“restores the middle class who promptly”**
  - sentence: …If successful, the LVT restores the middle class who promptly and rationally, repeal the LVT.…
  - why: The essay argues that successful LVT implementation creates a political coalition that repeals the tax, implying it is politically unstable without broader structural changes.

### [Ain't Got No Job](https://www.progress.org/articles/aint-got-no-job/)

  - sentence: …Eliminate all taxes and arbitrary restrictions on labor and enterprise. Get public revenue from land value, pollution charges, and user fees instead.…
  - why: The essay argues that shifting the tax burden off labor and onto land value eliminates involuntary unemployment, thereby raising productivity and employment.
- **supports** [`narratives/tax-land-not-labor`](https://progress.org/wiki/tax-land-not-labor/) — anchor: **“Eliminate all taxes and arbitrary restrictions on labor”**
  - sentence: …Eliminate all taxes and arbitrary restrictions on labor and enterprise. Get public revenue from land value, pollution charges, and user fees instead.…
  - why: The essay explicitly advocates for the Georgist fiscal shift of removing taxes on work to fund government through land value.
- **counters** [`objections/lvt-needs-zoning-reform-first`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-needs-zoning-reform-first/) — anchor: **“restrictions and taxes make it more costly”**
  - sentence: …The alternative to being an employee of others is to be self-employed, and here restrictions and taxes make it more costly and difficult to be your own boss.…
  - why: The essay identifies zoning and regulatory barriers—not just land tax policy—as primary causes of unemployment, implying that land value capture alone is insufficient without deregulation.

  - sentence: …Otherwise, more workers will get laid off and have a hard time finding work as we slide down the contracting phase of the business cycle.…
  - why: The essay documents rising unemployment and job losses as evidence of the recurring business cycle downturn.

  - why: The essay provides a concrete methodological response (sales validation) to the practical objection that land values cannot be accurately separated and assessed.

  - why: By introducing open-source tools to standardize the assessment process, the essay counters the fear that assessment is inherently subjective or prone to corruption.

  - why: The narrative portrays the speculative investment as a reckless gamble that leads to ruin, countering the idea that it performs a useful economic function.

### [Banks, Land, and the Institution of Private Landownership](https://www.progress.org/articles/banks-land-and-the-institution-of-private-landownership/)

  - why: supports the moral argument that land is a common inheritance rather than a product of individual labor

  - why: The essay uses Alaska's oil dividend as a primary example of a durable, working resource-rent dividend program.

  - why: The essay illustrates the narrative that common wealth belongs to citizens and should be distributed via dividends.

  - why: The essay cites Norway's sovereign wealth fund as evidence of successful high-rate capture of natural-resource rent.

### [Book Review: The Land Trap by Mike Bird](https://www.progress.org/articles/book-review-the-land-trap-by-mike-bird/)

  - why: The essay outlines a specific mechanism where financialized land speculation creates boom-bust cycles.
- **supports** [`narratives/the-rentier-economy`](https://progress.org/wiki/the-rentier-economy/) — anchor: **“Land outcompetes other assets as an investment”**
  - sentence: …Land outcompetes other assets as an investment Traditional investments like stocks, bonds, and going into business for yourself all contribute to the real economy by directing money towards tools, materials, research, and workers.…
  - why: The essay describes how land becomes the dominant asset class, crowding out productive investment.

  - why: The essay argues that banks are huge specifically because they profit from land via mortgages, supporting the claim that banking growth is land-credit driven.

  - sentence: …Most corporations are only so large because they profit from common wealth—from wealth that belongs to the people.…
  - why: The essay contends that corporate size and wealth derive from extracting value from the commons (land, nature) rather than productive activity, aligning with the claim that profits reflect economic re
- **supports** [`problems/high-land-rents-suppress-productivity`](https://progress.org/wiki/high-land-rents-suppress-productivity/) — anchor: **“forces people to look for jobs”**
  - sentence: …This forces people to look for jobs in order to pay the rent instead of allowing them (with more available cash and less risk) to engage in activities that create jobs for other people.…
  - why: The essay explains that land hoarding and rent burdens force workers into wage labor rather than entrepreneurial job creation, illustrating how high land rents suppress productivity and opportunity.

  - why: The essay describes a systemic flaw where the economy rewards corporations for extracting common wealth (rents) rather than adding value, which is the core definition of a rentier economy.

  - why: The essay summarizes the central mechanism of the Single Tax narrative—shifting all taxes to land rent.

  - sentence: …The residential dividend or Citizens Dividend turns land value into commonwealth.…
  - why: The essay advocates for sharing recovered rents as a dividend to align public interests with environmental preservation.

### [Earned Income and Unearned Income](https://www.progress.org/articles/earned-income-and-unearned-income/)
- **supports** [`narratives/unearned-increment-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/unearned-increment-narrative/) — anchor: **“earned income is wages”**
  - sentence: …At the roots, earned income is wages, and unearned income is land rent.…
  - why: The essay explicitly defines the core Georgist distinction that land rent is unearned income while wages are earned.
- **counters** [`objections/land-is-just-capital`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-is-just-capital/) — anchor: **“originating in labor and capital goods”**
  - sentence: …After having paid the land rent to the relevant community, none of the dividends include land rent. Therefore, originating in labor and capital goods, dividends are earned income.…
  - why: The essay argues that returns on capital are earned once land rent is separated, countering the claim that land is indistinguishable from capital.
- **supports** [`narratives/community-creates-land-value`](https://progress.org/wiki/community-creates-land-value/) — anchor: **“proper owners of the land rent”**
  - sentence: …If the people are equally the proper owners of the land rent, they deserve to receive it.…
  - why: The essay supports the narrative that the community, not the individual owner, is the proper recipient of land rent.
- **counters** [`objections/marshall-single-tax-objection`](https://progress.org/wiki/marshall-single-tax-objection/) — anchor: **“origin of the saved funds is wages”**
  - sentence: …The origin of the saved funds is wages, and the origin of the interest payment is wages. Therefore the interest income is wages.…
  - why: The essay refutes the idea that all asset returns are rent by distinguishing interest derived from wages (earned) from interest derived from rent (unearned).

  - why: The essay lists congestion charges as a primary category of efficient taxes that reduce economic harm.
- **supports** [`benefits/lvt-can-replace-capital-taxes-without-efficiency-loss`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-can-replace-capital-taxes-without-efficiency-loss/) — anchor: **“tapping of land value”**
  - sentence: …A simultaneous shift that decreases taxes on sales, income, and buildings while increasing levies on land value, pollution, and congestion would reduce pollution while increasing economic efficiency, raising profits and wages.…
  - why: The essay advocates replacing taxes on buildings and income with land value levies to eliminate deadweight loss and increase productivity.
- **supports** [`benefits/taxing-land-raises-productivity`](https://progress.org/wiki/taxing-land-raises-productivity/) — anchor: **“increase productivity and wages”**
  - sentence: …In fact, efficiency taxes would substantially increase productivity and wages.…
  - why: The essay contends that shifting to efficiency taxes, specifically land value taxes, raises productivity and wages by removing the excess burden of current taxes.

### [Fate of the Union 2015: More Bad Taxes](https://www.progress.org/articles/fate-of-the-union-2015-more-bad-taxes/)

  - sentence: …The money one pays for land is a subsidy to previous owners, and the rent one receives now, either explicitly in rental money, or implicitly in the rental value, is a subsidy from the rent generated by the community and its public goods.…
  - why: The essay directly states that land rent is generated by the community and public goods, which is the foundational argument of this claim.
- **supports** [`benefits/lvt-can-replace-capital-taxes-without-efficiency-loss`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-can-replace-capital-taxes-without-efficiency-loss/) — anchor: **“high tax rate on wages or investment income stifles”**
  - sentence: …On the other hand, a high tax rate on wages or investment income stifles work effort, entrepreneurship, and investment.…
  - why: The essay argues that taxing capital and labor harms economic productivity, implying that shifting to a base that does not stifle these factors (land) would improve welfare.

  - why: The author argues that Georgist remedies are fully achievable within a fiat money paradigm, countering the objection that LVT is useless without other structural reforms like zoning.
- **supports** [`narratives/single-tax-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/single-tax-narrative/) — anchor: **“taxes effectively create unemployment in the private sector”**
  - sentence: …Along with chartalism before it, MMT maintains the reason the currency has value is taxes effectively create unemployment in the private sector which the government then directs to the public purpose via spending.…
  - why: The essay discusses the functional necessity of taxes to drive currency demand, which relates to the Georgist narrative of replacing distortionary taxes with a single tax on land.

  - why: The essay illustrates the economic efficiency of countries specializing in natural resource extraction, which underpins the Georgist argument for capturing resource rents.

  - sentence: …This money is not free of special interests, as it comes from the greatest special interest of all, the ruling powers.…
  - why: The essay argues that concentrating rent revenue in government hands empowers the ruling elite, supporting the objection that public rent collection breeds corruption.
- **supports** [`narratives/tax-land-not-labor`](https://progress.org/wiki/tax-land-not-labor/) — anchor: **“tax on corporate profits acts”**
  - sentence: …But a tax on corporate profits acts like an addition to the costs of production, and some of the tax is passed on to those who buy the products.…
  - why: By highlighting the inefficiency and incidence of corporate taxes, the essay implicitly supports the narrative of shifting taxes onto inelastic bases like land.

### [Henry George in Favor of a Basic Income](https://www.progress.org/articles/henry-george-in-favor-of-a-basic-income/)

  - sentence: …We could divide this, if we wanted to, among the whole community, share and share alike.…

- **supports** [`problems/land-rent-could-fund-government`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-rent-could-fund-government/) — anchor: **“yield revenues even larger”**
  - sentence: …The taking for the use of the community of that value of privilege which attaches to the possession of land, would, wherever social development has advanced beyond a certain stage, yield revenues even larger than those now raised by taxatio…
  - why: George argues that capturing land rent would generate sufficient revenue to exceed current government needs, creating a surplus.
- **supports** [`benefits/rent-dividends-reduce-poverty`](https://progress.org/wiki/rent-dividends-reduce-poverty/) — anchor: **“secure from want”**

  - why: George proposes using the land rent fund to provide a basic income that would prevent poverty and want among the vulnerable.

  - sentence: …To take land values for public purposes is not really to impose a tax, but to take for public purposes a value created by the community.…
  - why: George justifies the dividend by asserting that land value is socially created, not earned by the individual owner.

### [Henry Plottre and the Magically Expanding Land](https://www.progress.org/articles/henry-plottre-and-the-magically-expanding-land/)
- **illustrates** [`benefits/lvt-dampens-land-speculation`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-dampens-land-speculation/) — anchor: **“those holding land idle”**
  - sentence: …When you collect the land rent like a bear collects honey, then those holding land idle will put it to good use so that it is worth paying the rent.…
  - why: The wizard's explanation that taxing land forces idle holders to use it illustrates the mechanism by which LVT dampens speculation.
- **illustrates** [`benefits/taxing-land-raises-productivity`](https://progress.org/wiki/taxing-land-raises-productivity/) — anchor: **“put it to good use”**
  - sentence: …When you collect the land rent like a bear collects honey, then those holding land idle will put it to good use so that it is worth paying the rent.…
  - why: The story equates putting idle land to good use with 'growing more land,' illustrating the Georgist claim that taxing land raises effective supply and productivity.
- **counters** [`objections/land-no-longer-matters`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-no-longer-matters/) — anchor: **“Land is fixed in supply”**

  - sentence: …“Tax the land,” said the wizard.…
  - why: The wizard's final prescription to 'Tax the land' as the secret to saving the world supports the narrative of shifting burdens to land.

  - sentence: …As real estate prices rise, helped by cheap credit and government spending, speculators jump in and help raise property values to a height making dwellings unaffordable.…
  - why: The essay explicitly describes the mechanism of the land cycle—cheap credit fueling speculation that drives up prices until the crash—vindicating the narrative.
- **supports** [`problems/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land`](https://progress.org/wiki/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land/) — anchor: **“increase in land rent”**
  - sentence: …The mother of all subsidies is the increase in land rent and land value caused by the public goods provided by government.…
  - why: The essay argues that public goods create land value, which constitutes a subsidy to owners, directly supporting the claim about public investment capitalizing into land.
- **supports** [`benefits/taxing-land-raises-productivity`](https://progress.org/wiki/taxing-land-raises-productivity/) — anchor: **“taxes were on land value”**
  - sentence: …There was no income or sales tax back then; taxes were on real estate, and with the buildings destroyed, in effect taxes were on land value.…
  - why: The essay uses the post-1906 San Francisco rapid recovery as historical evidence that taxing land value incentivizes rebuilding and productivity.
- **supports** [`narratives/tax-land-not-labor`](https://progress.org/wiki/tax-land-not-labor/) — anchor: **“taxes were on land value”**
  - sentence: …The same would happen today if the taxes were on land value instead of on labor, goods, and enterprise.…
  - why: The essay advocates for shifting the tax burden off labor and enterprise onto land value to improve the economy, which is the core of this narrative.

  - why: The essay proposes shifting the tax base from capital (VAT on goods) to land to eliminate deadweight loss and compensate for external trade barriers.

  - why: The essay explicitly grounds its argument for land rights on the premise that land value is created by the community and nature.

  - why: The essay argues for absolute possession rights conditional on rent payment, supporting the geoist remedy of secure tenure over state seizure.

  - why: The essay argues that possession remains secure if rent is paid, countering the objection that a full land tax claim destroys the owner's stake or the tax base.

### [How to Extirpate Poverty](https://www.progress.org/articles/how-to-extirpate-poverty/)

  - sentence: …As explained by the economist Henry George in his book Progress and Poverty, the margin of production moves out farther and faster to less productive land when people can hold land even if they don’t use it.…

  - why: The essay claims that collecting land rent forces land into its most productive use, thereby raising the wage level and economic output.

- **supports** [`narratives/tax-land-not-labor`](https://progress.org/wiki/tax-land-not-labor/) — anchor: **“taxes that come from wages”**
  - sentence: …This would involve a tax shift, in which taxes that come from wages are replaced by public revenue from land rent, or from voluntary payments by folks who receive an equal share of the rent.…
  - why: The essay advocates for an efficiency tax shift that removes levies on work and investment to fund government through land rent.

### [How to Solve the Credit Crisis](https://www.progress.org/articles/how-to-solve-the-credit-crisis/)

  - sentence: …The mortgage problem would be gone, as there would be no more mortgages on land.…
  - why: The essay identifies the credit crisis as fundamentally a mortgage problem tied to land, proposing to eliminate land mortgages to solve it.

- **illustrates** [`objections/lvt-transition-wealth-shock`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-transition-wealth-shock/) — anchor: **“compensate for the loss of selling price”**
